Density and Heights Chapter B
How to read the Density & Heights maps:
The core part of the strategy comprises four spatial zones across the city, determined by their relative
suitability for density and heights.
DENSITY HEIGHTS
FAR Dwellings Per Hectare No. of Storeys
Prevailing Target Prevailing Target * Prevailing Target
Lower Upper Lower Upper Lower Upper
CITY
Please Refer to
FRINGE / CORRIDOR / CENTRE
Cork City Development Plan 2022-2028
INNER URBAN SUBURBS (Volume 1)
OUTER SUBURBS
Where to find more information:
• These maps are based on the supporting document ‘Cork City Urban Density,
Building Height and Tall Building Study’
• D C e o t m ai m ls u o n n it i D es e ’ n i s n it V ie o s l u c m an e b 1 e . found in Chapter 3, ‘Delivering Homes and B B C u u o i i l r l d d k i i n C n g g it y S H t U e u i r d g b y h a t n a D nd en T s a it ll y ,
• Details on Cityscape and Building Height can be found in Chapter 11
‘Placemaking and Managing Development’ in Volume 1.
• Specific Density and Height for the Cork Docklands and Tivoli Docks
are set out in Chapter 10 ‘Key Growth Areas & Neighbourhood
Development Sites’ in Volume 1.

View Management Framework Chapter C
How to read the View Management Framework maps:
The core part of the strategy comprises four spatial zones across the city, determined by their relative
suitability for density and heights.
Legend
Strategic Landmark Building
Local Landmark Buildings
Strategic Viewing Locations
Strategic Linear Views
Viewing Location of linear views of special amenity value
Where to find more information:
• The policy framework for Cork City’s View Management Framework of views and prospects of special amenity
value is set out in Volume 1: Chapter 6: Green and Blue Infrastructure, Open Space and Biodiversity.
• The views are listed in Volume 3: Built Heritage Objectives.

Chapter D Docklands
How to read the South Docks Drainage Strategy map:
Cork City Council has prepared a South Docks Drainage and Levels Strategy (2022) to inform the
development of the City Docks The objective of the Strategy is to provide a long-term placemaking vision
that is flexible, environmentally responsible and climate-resilient, particularly to potential changes in sea level
and rainfall intensity. For more information refer to Volume 1 Chapter 10, subchapter 2 - City Docks.
This drawing should be read in conjunction with the South Docks Drainage Strategy Report.
Notes:
• The details of the proposed drainage and polder flood defence infrastructure are indicative and
are subject to detailed design.
• All design finished floor levels shall be informed by a Site-Specific Flood Risk Assessment in
accordance with “The Planning System and Flood Risk Management Guidelines for Planning Authorities”
(OPW/DoEHLG, 2009), undertaken by the Applicant at Development Management Stage.
• The proposed ground levels and finished floor levels have been developed on the assumption that the
proposed polder flood defences are in place and provide protection to the 1 in 200.

Chapter E Car Parking Zones
How to read the Car Parking Zone maps:
See Volume 1 Chapter 4 ‘Transport and Mobility’, Table 4.6 for the Primary areas to which the Parking
Zones relate.
See Chapter 11 Placemaking and Managing Development, Table 11.13 for details of Maximum Car
Parking Standards per Car Parking Zone.
Separate Parking Standards relate to Docklands and are unaffected by Variation No. 1, see Chapter 10
‘Key Growth Areas & Neighbourhood Development Sites’, Table 10.5, Table 10.17 and Table 10.18.
